============== task analysis ================
1. Extract and Summarize Given Information:
- The problem involves a tetrahedron named ABCD.
- Edge lengths are given with specific equalities:
  * AB = CD = √41
  * AC = BD = √80
  * BC = AD = √89
- There exists a point I inside the tetrahedron such that the perpendicular distances from I to each of the four faces of the tetrahedron are equal.
- The common distance from I to each face can be expressed in the form (m√n)/p, where m, n, p are positive integers, m and p are coprime, and n is square-free.

2. Analyze Relationships Between Components:
- The tetrahedron has pairs of edges equal in length, suggesting some symmetry or special geometric property.
- The equalities AB=CD, AC=BD, and BC=AD imply a certain pairing or correspondence between edges opposite or related in the tetrahedron.
- The point I is equidistant from all faces, meaning I is the incenter of the tetrahedron (the center of the inscribed sphere).
- The condition of equal distances to faces imposes constraints on the position of I and relates to the inradius of the tetrahedron.
- The problem likely involves using the given edge lengths to determine the volume and surface area or face areas to find the inradius.

3. Identify the Field of Study:
- The problem is primarily in the domain of solid geometry (3D Euclidean geometry).
- It involves concepts of tetrahedra, distances from points to planes, and properties of inscribed spheres.
- Subfields include metric geometry and possibly vector geometry or analytic geometry if coordinate methods are used.
- Such problems commonly appear in mathematical competitions and advanced geometry contexts.

4. Highlight Aspects Needing Clarification:
- The problem does not specify the coordinates or angles explicitly, so the tetrahedron's exact shape is not fully defined beyond edge lengths.
- It is assumed that the tetrahedron is non-degenerate and that the point I lies strictly inside.
- The symmetry in edge lengths suggests a special tetrahedron type, but this is not explicitly stated.
- Calculations involving the inradius may be complex due to the irrational edge lengths.
- No explicit mention of the method to find I or the inradius is given, which may require advanced geometric or algebraic techniques.

async def forward(self, taskInfo):
    from collections import Counter
    print("Task Requirement: ", taskInfo)
    sub_tasks = []
    agents = []
    logs = []

    cot_sc_instruction_1 = "Sub-task 1: Determine the areas of the four faces of tetrahedron ABCD using the given edge lengths and the symmetry conditions. Use the given edge lengths AB=CD=\u221A41, AC=BD=\u221A80, BC=AD=\u221A89 to find the areas of faces ABC, ABD, ACD, and BCD."
    N = self.max_sc
    cot_agents_1 = [LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Chain-of-Thought Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.0) for _ in range(N)]
    possible_answers_1 = []
    possible_thinkings_1 = []
    subtask_desc1 = {
        "subtask_id": "subtask_1",
        "instruction": cot_sc_instruction_1,
        "context": ["user query"],
        "agent_collaboration": "SC_CoT"
    }
    for i in range(N):
        thinking1, answer1 = await cot_agents_1[i]([taskInfo], cot_sc_instruction_1, is_sub_task=True)
        agents.append(f"CoT-SC agent {cot_agents_1[i].id}, determine face areas, thinking: {thinking1.content}; answer: {answer1.content}")
        possible_answers_1.append(answer1)
        possible_thinkings_1.append(thinking1)
    final_decision_agent_1 = LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Final Decision Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.0)
    thinking1, answer1 = await final_decision_agent_1([taskInfo] + possible_thinkings_1, "Sub-task 1: Synthesize and choose the most consistent and correct face areas for the tetrahedron.", is_sub_task=True)
    sub_tasks.append(f"Sub-task 1 output: thinking - {thinking1.content}; answer - {answer1.content}")
    subtask_desc1['response'] = {"thinking": thinking1, "answer": answer1}
    logs.append(subtask_desc1)
    print("Step 1: ", sub_tasks[-1])

    cot_sc_instruction_2 = "Sub-task 2: Compute the volume of tetrahedron ABCD using the given edge lengths and the derived face areas from Sub-task 1. Use appropriate geometric relations or formulas to find the volume."
    cot_agents_2 = [LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Chain-of-Thought Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.0) for _ in range(N)]
    possible_answers_2 = []
    possible_thinkings_2 = []
    subtask_desc2 = {
        "subtask_id": "subtask_2",
        "instruction": cot_sc_instruction_2,
        "context": ["user query", thinking1.content],
        "agent_collaboration": "SC_CoT"
    }
    for i in range(N):
        thinking2, answer2 = await cot_agents_2[i]([taskInfo, thinking1], cot_sc_instruction_2, is_sub_task=True)

        possible_answers_2.append(answer2)
        possible_thinkings_2.append(thinking2)
    final_decision_agent_2 = LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Final Decision Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.0)
    thinking2, answer2 = await final_decision_agent_2([taskInfo] + possible_thinkings_2, "Sub-task 2: Synthesize and choose the most consistent and correct volume for the tetrahedron.", is_sub_task=True)
    sub_tasks.append(f"Sub-task 2 output: thinking - {thinking2.content}; answer - {answer2.content}")
    subtask_desc2['response'] = {"thinking": thinking2, "answer": answer2}
    logs.append(subtask_desc2)
    print("Step 2: ", sub_tasks[-1])

    debate_instr_3 = "Sub-task 3: Calculate the inradius of the tetrahedron, i.e., the common distance from point I to each face, using the volume and total surface area (sum of face areas) obtained from Sub-tasks 1 and 2. Given solutions to the problem from other agents, consider their opinions as additional advice. Please think carefully and provide an updated answer."
    debate_agents_3 = [LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Debate Agent", model=self.node_model, role=role, temperature=0.0) for role in self.debate_role]
    N_max_3 = self.max_round
    all_thinking3 = [[] for _ in range(N_max_3)]
    all_answer3 = [[] for _ in range(N_max_3)]
    subtask_desc3 = {
        "subtask_id": "subtask_3",
        "instruction": debate_instr_3,
        "context": ["user query", thinking1.content, thinking2.content],
        "agent_collaboration": "Debate"
    }
    for r in range(N_max_3):
        for i, agent in enumerate(debate_agents_3):
            if r == 0:
                thinking3, answer3 = await agent([taskInfo, thinking1, thinking2], debate_instr_3, r, is_sub_task=True)
            else:
                input_infos_3 = [taskInfo, thinking1, thinking2] + all_thinking3[r-1]
                thinking3, answer3 = await agent(input_infos_3, debate_instr_3, r, is_sub_task=True)

            all_thinking3[r].append(thinking3)

    final_decision_agent_3 = LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Final Decision Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.0)

    sub_tasks.append(f"Sub-task 3 output: thinking - {thinking3.content}; answer - {answer3.content}")

    thinking4, answer4 = await final_decision_agent_4([taskInfo] + possible_thinkings_4, "Sub-task 4: Synthesize and choose the most consistent and correct simplified form and sum.", is_sub_task=True)
    sub_tasks.append(f"Sub-task 4 output: thinking - {thinking4.content}; answer - {answer4.content}")

    return final_answer, logs

============== high level task decomposition ================
[{'objective': 'Calculate the area of each face of the tetrahedron using the given edge lengths'}, {'objective': 'Compute the volume of the tetrahedron from the given edge lengths'}, {'objective': 'Sum the areas of all faces to find the total surface area'}, {'objective': 'Calculate the inradius using the formula inradius = 3 * volume / total surface area and simplify the result'}]
============== task analysis ================
1. Extract and Summarize Given Information:
- The problem involves a tetrahedron named ABCD.
- Edge lengths are given with specific equalities:
  * AB = CD = √41
  * AC = BD = √80
  * BC = AD = √89
- There exists a point I inside the tetrahedron such that the perpendicular distances from I to each of the four faces are equal.
- The common distance from I to each face can be expressed in the form (m√n)/p, where m, n, p are positive integers, m and p are coprime, and n is square-free.

2. Analyze Relationships Between Components:
- The tetrahedron has pairs of edges equal in length, suggesting some symmetry or special geometric property.
- The equalities AB=CD, AC=BD, and BC=AD imply a certain pairing or correspondence between edges opposite or related in the tetrahedron.
- The point I is equidistant from all faces, indicating that I is the incenter of the tetrahedron (the center of the inscribed sphere).
- The problem’s structure relies on the relationship between edge lengths and the inradius (distance from I to faces).
- The constraints on m, n, p indicate the final answer should be simplified to lowest terms with n square-free.

3. Identify the Field of Study:
- The problem is primarily in the domain of solid geometry (3D Euclidean geometry).
- It involves concepts of tetrahedra, distances from points to planes, and properties of incenters and inscribed spheres.
- Algebraic manipulation and possibly vector geometry or coordinate geometry may be involved.
- Such problems are common in mathematical competitions and advanced geometry studies.

4. Highlight Aspects Needing Clarification:
- The problem does not specify the coordinates or angles explicitly, so the tetrahedron’s exact shape is inferred only from edge lengths.
- It is assumed that the tetrahedron is non-degenerate and that the point I lies strictly inside.
- The uniqueness of point I as the incenter is implied but not explicitly stated.
- Calculating the inradius from given edge lengths can be complex, involving volume and face areas, which are not provided.
- Potential challenges include verifying the tetrahedron’s existence with given edge lengths and computing the inradius without additional data.
